<div id="review_134566353" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/134566353" />
    <a title="Rachel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/298806-rachel"><img alt="Rachel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452743476p2/298806.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/134566353?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel" href="/user/show/298806-rachel">Rachel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/298806-rachel?shelf=2011-debut-author-challenge">2011-debut-author-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/298806-rachel?shelf=galley-grab">galley-grab</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer134566353" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6697275312322959925">When her stepmother gets a job in New York City, sixteen-year-old Violet McKenna is forced to choose whether to to go with her or stay with her Grandmother. Although Atlanta is her home, and her Gran her only real family, Violet is inexplicably drawn to Winterhaven, an elite boarding school in Tarrytown, New York.<br/><br/>For the first time since her father’s death she feels like just maybe things will be okay. Winterhaven is a place where she can start over, where no one knows about her premonitions, an</span>
  <span id="freeText6697275312322959925" style="display:none">When her stepmother gets a job in New York City, sixteen-year-old Violet McKenna is forced to choose whether to to go with her or stay with her Grandmother. Although Atlanta is her home, and her Gran her only real family, Violet is inexplicably drawn to Winterhaven, an elite boarding school in Tarrytown, New York.<br /><br />For the first time since her father’s death she feels like just maybe things will be okay. Winterhaven is a place where she can start over, where no one knows about her premonitions, and she will be able to fit in and shed her freak status once and for all.<br /><br />If she had only listened to her gut she would have realized right away that Winterhaven was not a normal school and that her flashes of the future were only one of the many types of “gifts” that the students possessed – telekinesis, clairsentience and astral projection to name just a few others. Only shape-shifting labeled you an outcast at Winterhaven.<br /><br />Even in a school filled with the psychically gifted, there was something different about Aidan Gray. Something that made him stand apart from all the other students. Something that drew Violet to him. Her friends called it the “Aidan effect,” but it wasn’t just attraction. Even with the intensity of his gaze, from eyes that were more blue than grey, eyes that captivated her, there was something about him that scared her.<br /><br />But when her nightmarish visions, visions that foretold of her father’s death, become about him, she knows that she must do whatever she can to change the course of that future. Even if it means turning her back on her destiny.<br /><br />***<br /><br />Haven is an enchanting first book in this new series and a story that readers will instantly fall in love with. It has such a wonderful, easygoing flow, making this an uncomplicated and totally entertaining read.<br /><br />There is a nice mix of personalities among the characters that the author has created, even though the focus is on the two main characters – Violet and Aidan. While Haven doesn’t fully delve into each character’s abilities or background, more than enough information is given to get a clear picture of who these secondary characters are. And as this is a series, there is likely to be much more revealed in books to come.<br /><br />There is also a good span of time in which the book takes place that lets the plot progress naturally. This length of time allows the relationship between Violet and Aidan to have its ups and downs in a much more realistic way, without feeling jam-packed into the typical few weeks that are common in many series books.<br /><br />It is easy to just relax into this book and let the story take you on its journey. There are no extreme highs or lows, no love triangle and no cliffhanger ending, but there is mystery, suspense and a climactic conclusion that will keep you engrossed.<br /><br />Author Kristi Cook does a wonderful job of setting up the world and characters for this series. And notwithstanding some similarities with other books in this genre, this is a book that has its own identity.<br /><br />With a number of unanswered questions and directions that the story can go in future books, there is also still much to learn about Violet and her abilities, Aidan and his past, Violet’s friends and the one thing that all the students at Winterhaven have in common, except Jack.<br /><br />On a personal note:<br /><br />It was just so easy to love this book. It flowed so well I didn’t even realize I was reading, I was so immersed in this story. Even though it is just over four hundred pages, I blinked and was practically finished reading it. The story just flew by.<br /><br />Of course I would have loved to see some of the spaces in the timeline filled in with more of everything, like Violet’s fencing matches, Aidan’s experiments and disappearances, and stories about Violet’s friends – even the trip to St. Bart’s and the unfortunate sunburn. But then it would have been a six hundred plus page story and nothing would be saved for the sequel.<br /><br />Even though I like Violet, I still don’t know enough about her yet to promote her to my favorite character in this series. Currently, Kate is my favorite female character in this book. (And it’s not just because she’s with a guy named Jack and I’m a Lost fan.) I just think telekinesis is cool. And the fact that she uses it for the most trivial of reasons makes her all the more likable.<br /><br />And although many may think that Aidan is a bit of a jerk, I’m on the fence, but leaning toward “good guy.” Most of his behavior is completely understandable, except for the picture. (And I won’t say more for fear of revealing too much.)<br /><br />I will definitely be reading all future books in this series. No doubt about it. And I am a new Kristi Cook fan.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6697275312322959925" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_322862805" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/322862805" />
    <a title="Rachel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5306375-rachel"><img alt="Rachel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588353687p2/5306375.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/322862805?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel" href="/user/show/5306375-rachel">Rachel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5306375-rachel?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer322862805" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13379602128943725090">A list of things I love in books:<br/>-Boarding schools<br/>-Teenagers with psychic powers<br/>-Cute boys<br/>-Awesome protagonists<br/>-Romance that's not too perfect to be believable<br/>-Funny and lovable groups of friends<br/><br/>Guess what? This book has ALL OF THE THINGS. ALL OF THEM.<br/><br/>And guess what it also has? Vampires. And guess what I'm generally not a huge fan of? Vampires. And guess what was done really well in this book so that even a non-vampire fan like me could enjoy it immensely? YOU GUESSED IT, VAMPIRES.<br/><br/>But hold on. </span>
  <span id="freeText13379602128943725090" style="display:none">A list of things I love in books:<br />-Boarding schools<br />-Teenagers with psychic powers<br />-Cute boys<br />-Awesome protagonists<br />-Romance that's not too perfect to be believable<br />-Funny and lovable groups of friends<br /><br />Guess what? This book has ALL OF THE THINGS. ALL OF THEM.<br /><br />And guess what it also has? Vampires. And guess what I'm generally not a huge fan of? Vampires. And guess what was done really well in this book so that even a non-vampire fan like me could enjoy it immensely? YOU GUESSED IT, VAMPIRES.<br /><br />But hold on. Lemme back up a bit.<br /><br />So this book has a lovely main character named Violet who I really love because she is really normal and easy to relate to. She's not all OH LOOK HOW BADASS I AM I'M GOING TO SHOOT ARROWS AND KILL THINGS GRRR, but she's also not all Um hi I'm really shy and quiet and kind of plain and unremarkable and I'll just let the hot guys swoop in and save me, thanks. Violet is a very healthy balance between those two levels, a balance that I think is what most girls are actually like. So I love her, obviously. <br /><br />The book starts with Violet's first day at a new boarding school. She's the new kid who's never really been anywhere outside the town she lived in her whole life, and on top of that, she's still reeling from the death of her father. So that's pretty stressful, right?<br /><br /><br />Well, things get even more stressful. NO SPOILERS NO SPOILERS, but yeah, things happen and let me just say again how much I love Violet. She handles everything in a really normal way. She's not too strong, but not too weak. HEALTHY BALANCE, PEOPLE. I LOVE IT.<br /><br /><br />And so then there's a plot and stuff, with people and things. DON'T ROLL YOUR EYES. I'M JUST TRYING TO REMAIN SPOILER-FREE. FOR YOUR BENEFIT OF COURSE. Also because I have no idea how to sum up all the awesomeness that happens.<br /><br />Anyway, one of my FAVORITE things about this book is THE GROUP OF FRIENDS. Because you know what's missing in a lot of YA books? A lovely little group of really close girlfriends who are funny and nice and loyal and who the main character can have fun with and also share their secrets with. Why don't we have more friendships like this in books? Violet grows close to four girls, and instead of just being there for comic relief or whatever, these friends are important characters who are helpful in situations and really add to the story. AND I LOVE IT. *hugs ALL THE CHARACTERS*<br /><br />And vampires. There are teenagers with psychic powers, which is weird enough, BUT THERE ARE ALSO VAMPIRES. It's just so epic. And to be honest, there are very few vampire books that I actually like. But the vampire mythology and stuff was done really well in Haven, and I am seriously impressed.<br />Also, it's me, so obviously I'm going to talk about THE BOY. I'm a big fan of THE BOY. His name is Aidan. He's kinda mysterious. And hot. I like him a lot.<br /><br />The relationship between Violet and Aidan has a whole lot of issues, but it's still believable and realistic. They fight and break up and kiss and make up and fight some more and kiss some more and they're always up and down and back and forth and it's not perfect but that makes it even better.<br /><br />I mean, I think I'd be a better match for Aidan than Violet but WHATEVER IT'S NOT LIKE IT BOTHERS ME OR ANYTHING. I'LL BE FINE DON'T WORRY.<br /><br />*clears throat* So yeah. I pretty much love everything about this book. And I would not have read this if I had not gone to Books of Wonder a few days or weeks ago (I don't know how long ago it was. Don't judge. I STILL THINK IT'S NOVEMBER, OKAY?!) and met Kristi Cook, along with Amy Plum and Jocelyn Davies.<br /><br />I'm really glad I went to that event because it was really fun and now I have pretty signed books. Also I discovered Haven and fell in love with it and chatted with amazing authors and ate yummy food, so yeah.<br /><br />Wow. This ramble is ridiculously long and CAPSLOCK-y and just so crazy and unprofessional, even by my standards. I'm sorry I'm not sorry.<br /><br />MY POINT is that you should read this book, because I really like it, and so you should too. Also I would like the sequel now, please. Thank you.<br /><br />More insane rambling like this over at readwriteramble.blogspot.com</span>
  <a data-text-id="13379602128943725090" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_139129123" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/139129123" />
    <a title="Jessica (a GREAT read)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3549629-jessica-a-great-read"><img alt="Jessica (a GREAT read)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597965658p2/3549629.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/139129123?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica (a GREAT read)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica (a GREAT read)" href="/user/show/3549629-jessica-a-great-read">Jessica (a GREAT read)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139129123" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6259244617615016108">I received this E-ARC from Simon & Schuster.<br/><br/>Well I can honestly say that this was an okay read. Haven is Kristi Cook's debut in the YA genre and I had heard about it through the blogging world and it sounded interesting. And it was, mildly so.<br/><br/>I hate having to talk bad about books, it's really hard and I know everyone's opinions differ. So let me just state that this is my opinion. Others may find that they like the sound of the story, read and love it still and that's cool.<br/><br/>The book started off a</span>
  <span id="freeText6259244617615016108" style="display:none">I received this E-ARC from Simon &amp; Schuster.<br /><br />Well I can honestly say that this was an okay read. Haven is Kristi Cook's debut in the YA genre and I had heard about it through the blogging world and it sounded interesting. And it was, mildly so.<br /><br />I hate having to talk bad about books, it's really hard and I know everyone's opinions differ. So let me just state that this is my opinion. Others may find that they like the sound of the story, read and love it still and that's cool.<br /><br />The book started off a little slow, I mean it did start with Violet going to the new school, but it took her awhile to figure out this big secret about the school. As the BOC says, everyone there has gifts, and for some reason it takes Violet a little while to realize this. A day really, and there were all these subtle hints at it too. I don't know sometimes I felt she was a little slow on the uptake.<br /><br />The mystery elements were built up sort of well. Like the mysterious guy she has visions about, Aidan. It soon becomes apparent, to me at least, what his "gifts" are. But it takes Violet a little longer, again, to realize it, and then she doesn't really believe him right away. I mean that part was a little much in my opinion. That here she is at a school with kids with psychic talents and some are shapeshifters--not necessarily animal ones, but still. There are subtle hints to Aidan's identity that I was surprised it took her so long to figure it out and then to be in denial? After everything she's learned? That was a bit much too.<br /><br />The book also jumped from point to point a little fast at times. In one paragraph Violet would be saying Spring Break is in two weeks...then blah blah. The next paragraph jumps to her coming BACK from spring break. While it wasn't hard to follow it was just some serious time jumping in my opinion.<br /><br />There were a few other surprises towards the end as well that were somewhat shocking. But also felt forced in some ways. I just don't know what to think of it really.<br /><br />Violet was an okay character as well. Sure I thought she was a little dense at times, like she should have realized something was off here and there. But I can understand in some ways why she wanted to cling to the reality that she knew. But since that reality was already challenged and forfeited earlier on I thought she would be more accepting of other surprises.<br /><br />And there is a romance between Violet and a certain character, but it definitely rings too much of another novel that kind of irritated me a bit. I mean in some ways it is just the standard paranormal YA love thing, but still it was too much like said other book in my mind.<br /><br />Overall I have to give the book 2.5/5 stars. It wasn't horribly dreadful. I just got annoyed a little too often with certain things. I really hate having to talk bad about books, especially new ones, but Haven really just wasn't my style. It did have its good parts occasionally but nearly enough for my liking.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6259244617615016108" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_229385566" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/229385566" />
    <a title="Parametric" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4128204-parametric"><img alt="Parametric" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/229385566?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Parametric" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Parametric" href="/user/show/4128204-parametric">Parametric</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer229385566" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15900962897934757549">Let's play spot the book!<br/><br/>On her first day at her new school, the new girl encounters an incredibly gorgeous guy who is instantly and inexplicably fascinated by her. All the girls lust after him, but he has no time for anybody else. He is very pale, and his skin is icy cold. He can read her mind. He carries her around. He can move supernaturally fast, covering miles in seconds. Oh, and he's a <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[vampire. An immortal vampire. Who keeps repeating high school. And they can't be together </span></span>
  <span id="freeText15900962897934757549" style="display:none">Let's play spot the book!<br /><br />On her first day at her new school, the new girl encounters an incredibly gorgeous guy who is instantly and inexplicably fascinated by her. All the girls lust after him, but he has no time for anybody else. He is very pale, and his skin is icy cold. He can read her mind. He carries her around. He can move supernaturally fast, covering miles in seconds. Oh, and he's a <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[vampire. An immortal vampire. Who keeps repeating high school. And they can't be together (if you know what I mean) because he might snap and kill her at any moment.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight__Twilight___1_" title="Twilight (Twilight, #1) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Twilight</a>? Nope - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7141621.Haven__Winterhaven___1_" title="Haven (Winterhaven, #1) by Kristi Cook" rel="nofollow noopener">Haven</a>.<br /><br />Let's try again. A girl moves to a new town where she meets an incredibly gorgeous guy who turns out to be an immortal vampire. Unfortunately, she's a vampire slayer, the one girl in all the world (well, one of the three girls) who can protect humanity from vampires. They train together and fall in love, but their kinds are mortal enemies, and the girl fears that she will eventually have to kill her beloved. Oh, and the vampire is several hundred years old. And British. And was turned by a powerful female vampire who is still around.<br /><br />Early seasons of Buffy? Nope - still Haven.<br /><br />I love schools of magic in fiction, but I found Haven an uninspired redo of familiar tropes. The heroine Violet seems to have inherited the vampire-slaying role of a Buffy Summers without any of the necessary strength of will. Half the time she can hardly stand up, much less act; her legs are always buckling, her knees constantly weak. When she's attacked, she freezes up, then faints. She refuses to train as a slayer; in one particularly frustrating scene, hero Aidan is trying to teach her to save innocent lives by staking vampires, but she can't think about anything except his "sculpted" chest. Even at the climax, when it looks like Violet might be forced to actually do something, she's rescued by an unexpected character using a power never previously mentioned. It's a major deus ex machina. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I did enjoy Violet's army of girl friends, but ultimately, Buffy did this better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15900962897934757549" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_143907760" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/143907760" />
    <a title="All Things Urban Fantasy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2732683-all-things-urban-fantasy"><img alt="All Things Urban Fantasy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1320345194p2/2732683.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/143907760?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="All Things Urban Fantasy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="All Things Urban Fantasy" href="/user/show/2732683-all-things-urban-fantasy">All Things Urban Fantasy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2732683-all-things-urban-fantasy?shelf=reviewed-by-abigail">reviewed-by-abigail</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2732683-all-things-urban-fantasy?shelf=earc">earc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer143907760" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1309458048682145328">Review courtesy of All Things Urban Fantasy<br/><br/>I hate this cover. And not because it’s dull, plain, and uninspiring (I still have no idea why there’s a giant butterfly on the front). I hate it because it completely turned me off of this book so that I almost didn’t read it. And then I would have missed out on a story that is deeply romantic and tragic in a way that pierces your heart and makes you long for the impossible.<br/> <br/>HAVEN doesn’t really break new grown with it’s plot, in fact it borrows heavil</span>
  <span id="freeText1309458048682145328" style="display:none">Review courtesy of All Things Urban Fantasy<br /><br />I hate this cover. And not because it’s dull, plain, and uninspiring (I still have no idea why there’s a giant butterfly on the front). I hate it because it completely turned me off of this book so that I almost didn’t read it. And then I would have missed out on a story that is deeply romantic and tragic in a way that pierces your heart and makes you long for the impossible.<br /> <br />HAVEN doesn’t really break new grown with it’s plot, in fact it borrows heavily from Buffy, THE VAMPIRE DIARIES, TWILIGHT, FALLEN, and to a lesser degree HARRY POTTER and X-Men. But it does combine some of the best parts of those stories to create a book that plucks at your heartstrings, carries you along a dark romance, forces you to chase after a dangerous mystery, and holds you hostage until the very end.<br /> <br />What HAVEN doesn’t borrow are the clichés that litter this genre. We are spared the vicious beautiful clique at the boarding school where Violet transfers. She doesn’t get a long with everyone, but there aren’t any psycho cheerleaders who get off on torturing people. Better still, Violet isn’t some wimpy waif who needs to be coddled into using her abilities. And her love interest, Aiden…it’s impossible to say what I liked so much about him without giving away anything, but the way his maturity is explained so perfectly sidesteps something that always bothers me in YA fiction that I actually let out a sigh of relief.<br /> <br />Bad cover art can’t really be blamed on the author, and I hope readers will look past it and experience the story and characters inside because Paranormal YA doesn’t get much better than HAVEN. Mystery, romance, and friendship tied up in a neat paranormal package. On her website, Kristi says that HAVEN is the first in a planned trilogy. They can’t come soon enough.<br /><br />Sexual Content: <br />Kissing. References to sex.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1309458048682145328" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('FxU7oG9Q8e5vp4XQ4i3EgujJtwgRAcMw2RwD76ydTBo+NGNrBEzpBNM4qrtE+xbA4jjC/urEx7VQTBVO9h1rkg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('etDW7CGegfeF2wzxoqlFJTnjku+3vwMMZNaBxLp8EBVT8Y4nSoKZHTlEI5oEf5dnMxLnGUx6B4nthpdl4Pw3nQ==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10532556856538300230">New York Times bestselling YA author Kristi Cook is a transplanted southern gal who lives in New York City with her husband and two kids. Her YA debut, HAVEN, was released in Feb. 2011 by Simon Pulse. The last two volumes in the Winterhaven series, MIRAGE and ETERNAL, followed in 2012 and 2013. Her first contemporary, southern-set YA, MAGNOLIA, was released in 2014. She's currently working on a co</span>
  <span id="freeText10532556856538300230" style="display:none">New York Times bestselling YA author Kristi Cook is a transplanted southern gal who lives in New York City with her husband and two kids. Her YA debut, HAVEN, was released in Feb. 2011 by Simon Pulse. The last two volumes in the Winterhaven series, MIRAGE and ETERNAL, followed in 2012 and 2013. Her first contemporary, southern-set YA, MAGNOLIA, was released in 2014. She's currently working on a contemporary YA with paranormal elements set in Savannah, GA. <br /><br />Kristi also writes adult romantic fiction as Kristina Cook and Kristi Astor. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10532556856538300230" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
